GAME-THEORY MODEL (a microeconomics view of FJSP)
-------------------------------------------------
  Player      : a job - the decision-maker
  Strategy    : its machine choice per operation + its dispatch positions
  Payoff      : U_i = 1/(1 + a*C_i + b*W_i + g*Conf_i + d*Cmax)  (higher = better)
  Game        : all jobs competing for the shared machines
  Solution    : the decoded schedule once every job fixes its strategy
  Equilibrium : a stable schedule where no job can raise its payoff alone
Two jobs interact whenever their operations meet on the same machine: the
earlier one delays the other, so each job re-routes / re-sequences to raise
its OWN payoff, and the schedule settles at an equilibrium.

MODEL
-----
ONE payoff function. Each job is a self-interested player; machines are
shared resources the jobs compete for. Job i's payoff is
    U_i = 1 / ( 1 + a*C_i + b*W_i + g*Conf_i + d*Cmax )
with C_i = completion, W_i = waiting (= C_i - processing), Conf_i =
machine-conflict load (busier chosen machines cost more), and Cmax the
shared makespan that links each job's payoff to global quality. A schedule
is a Nash equilibrium when no job can raise U_i by changing its own
machine assignment or sequence position alone. The reported social
objective is the makespan Cmax.

Search: critical-path best-response with SINGLE-JOB and JOB-vs-JOB moves +
fictitious-play belief learning + Global/Local greedy seeding +
iterated local search + multiple runs.
Run 0 starts from a fully RANDOM profile; later runs are seeded by the
players' learned beliefs and greedy heuristics. Each step makes the best
deviation - a single job re-routing/re-sequencing, or two rival jobs that
share a machine swapping order or rerouting together - until neither any
job nor any rival pair can improve (a pairwise Nash-stable schedule). The
single best run is reported below. A single payoff drives everything.

TWO-PLAYER INTERACTION MOVES (which two jobs clashed, the change, the benefit)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Filtered from the trace above: only the moves where TWO rival jobs that share a
machine act together. 'swap' = the two jobs exchange order on the contested
machine; 'mutual' = both reroute off it. Such a move is accepted only when it
lowers the shared makespan Cmax, so it shows exactly how resolving the clash
benefits the players. C = a job's completion time (lower = better payoff).

TWO-PLAYER INTERACTIONS (who delays whom & how each strategy pays off)
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Two jobs INTERACT when their operations land on the same machine: the earlier
one holds the resource and DELAYS the later one. 'Delay' = how long the later
job was already ready but had to wait while the machine finished the rival's
operation. (*) marks a pair on the critical path - that exact rivalry is what
fixes the makespan Cmax, so resolving it is how the players reach the optimum.

PER-MACHINE TWO-PLAYER NASH GAMES (payoff tables, by machine section)
--------------------------------------------------------------------
For every machine where two jobs are rivals at the equilibrium, here is the
full normal-form game between those two players: rows/columns are the machines
each rival could route its contested operation to, and each cell is the pair of
payoffs (U_A, U_B) that results when all other players keep their strategies.
The played cell is (*); a pure-strategy Nash equilibrium is [NE]. This is where
you can read whether the two players are individually in equilibrium per machine.

====================================================================
Machine M1  -  TWO-PLAYER GAME
  Player 1 = J3  (operation O(3,4))
  Player 2 = J14  (operation O(14,2))
  critical-path rivalry: this clash is what fixes the makespan Cmax
====================================================================

(1) PAYOFF BIMATRIX   (each cell = payoff of Player 1 , payoff of Player 2)
  +-------------+------------------------+------------------------+
  | Job1 \ Job2 | Job2: M3               | Job2: M1               |
  +-------------+------------------------+------------------------+
  | Job1: M1    | 0.0038, 0.0032         | 0.0040, 0.0033 * NASH  |
  | Job1: M4    | 0.0036, 0.0031         | 0.0036, 0.0031         |
  +-------------+------------------------+------------------------+
  legend:  *  = cell the solver actually plays    NASH = pure-strategy Nash equilibrium

(2) PAYOFF CALCULATION   (how each cell above is obtained)
  U_i = 1 / (1 + a*C_i + b*W_i + g*Conf_i + d*Cmax)   with  a=1.0000  b=0.3000  g=0.0500  d=0.5000
  strategy pair           C_J3    C_J14   Cmax    U_J3      U_J14     note
  J3:M1 & J14:M3          88      129     191     0.0038    0.0032    
  J3:M1 & J14:M1          81      124     177     0.0040    0.0033    played Nash
  J3:M4 & J14:M3          92      135     198     0.0036    0.0031    
  J3:M4 & J14:M1          92      136     201     0.0036    0.0031    

(3) NASH CALCULATION   (iterated best response - how the equilibrium is selected)
  Step 1 - Player 1 (J3)'s best reply to each move of Player 2:
      if J14 plays M3  ->  J3's best = M1   (U_J3=0.0038)
      if J14 plays M1  ->  J3's best = M1   (U_J3=0.0040)
  Step 2 - Player 2 (J14)'s best reply to each move of Player 1:
      if J3 plays M1  ->  J14's best = M1   (U_J14=0.0033)
